" Liwet Chamberlain s~Ojh'ci>, London, January Oth, 182T.

SIR,
I am authorized by the H,ord Chamberlain
to acquaint you, that the King, taking into his beneficeut
consideration the very great distress which the shutting
Rp the Theatres for any length of time would occasion
to numerous Families, His Majesty has been graciously
pleased to command that the closing the Theatre under
your management on account of the melancholy event of
the demise of His Royal Highness the Duke of York,
shall be contined to this evening, the two days of the
JBody lying in state, and the day ot the Funeral, of which
due notice will be given."
I am, Sir,
Your obedient Servant,
J B. MASH
To the Manager of the)
Theatre-Roy at.

WITH FEELINGS OF THE TRUEST GRATITUDE AND RESPECT,

Mr. Brunton

(LATE MANAGER OF THIS THEATRE)
Returns his .ineerest and most heartfelt thanks to his Patrons and Friends for the many
Savour, and constant support with which they have uniformly honored him-Circumstaoces,
over which he could have no controul, have prevented his appearance before those
PATRONS AND FRIENDS for the LAST TWO YEARS, and in now presenting
himself to their notice FOR ONE NIGHT ONLY, he anxiously hopes he shall not be
teemed guilty of presumption in announcing THAT ONE NIGHT for HIS BENEFIT,
ind respectfully intreating a continuation of that Patronage it has ever been his greatest
pride and endeavour to merit,

i river that discharges itself into the sea, not fur from Carthage, is said by many authors to have there mot with it
•onstious Serpent, of 120 feet long, which much infested his .tiny, seizing his men. and swallowing them whole,

rioretta, Mrs. J K I F K R S O N .

The pastoral Opera of R O S I N A is in rehearsal, and
will be shortly revived. It lias been critically remarked
the! Rosin a is one of those graceful entertainments where
the characters, the lauguage, and the music all conspire to
please. It is written by a lady, and does honour to her
taste and genius. The story is borrowed from that of
Thomson's " Palemon and jLavinia" or the Scriptural one
of " BOAZ and RUTH?
It is purely pastoral, and leaves
upon the mind a pleasing impression of the simplicity and
innocence of that Golden Age which poets have been wont
to describe. The music of Shield gave a charm to this
Opera that will never wear away. It is impossible to conceive any thing more beautiful than its sweet and simple
melody.

Witt be |tfMMit«.i the eelefcfiatai Brais*, taken from Bulwer's admired Novel, called .

EUGENE
ARAN! :

OR, ST. ROBERT'S CAVE.
It i« scarcely necessary to remark that this Drama is extracted almost literally from the celebrated N o v e l ; *
work that, fur intensity of interest, masterly conception of character, power of language, beauty and effect, will
rarely find its parallel. The adaptor has only deviated from the original when obliged by stage necessity, and has
never reported to his own language when he could avail himself of that uf the novelist. That the drama was
highly successful, formed of materials so redolent of thrilling effect and breathless interest as those afforded by
H4r. BitUer's novel, can be no matter of wonder; the dramatio power and excessive skill displayed by Mr.
Bulwer in the management of his story, would have proved the adaptor to be a dullard indeed if be had not successfully availed himself of the advantages offered him.

The Field of 4D Footsteps
Is in preparation and will speedily be produced.
About .HI years ago, tradition gave the above name to one of the pasture fields at the back of the east side
uf Gower-street, in the immediate vicinity of Blooinsbury.square, called " the Long Fields," lying between
Tottenham Court Itoad and a rustic lane, eastward, which ran from the top of Southampton Road towards
Hampstead. They are now completely built upon, and the first stone of the London University was laid at the
north-westetm extremity of the only remaining remnant of " the Long Fields."
ft must tie known to many of the Inhabitant.; of the neighbourhood, that, in one of those fields the marks,
<is it of human footsteps, presented themselves, bearing the appearance of a regular advance and refloat of the
persons engaged in mortal combat; and, although the grass stood high and rich oil all the vest of the ground, not
a blade grew on the apparent footsteps. This strife, as the tradition states, was between two brothers, botfc of
whom perished I and took place during the time of the Commonwealth. Upon a brief memorial of thi. story and
* leading incident in a popular Scotch novel, the Drama, presented to the Public is founded.
The historical incident, also, is well authenticated : that the escape of the Duke of Glo'ster io his Mother.
Queen Henrietta, in France, was connived at by Oliver Cromwell.
